href="#cite_note-The_Economist-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> (in 2017 and 2019) at general election time in Britain, and both <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a> and <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> candidates in the United States. <i>Economist.com</i> puts its stance this way:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>What, besides free trade and free markets, does <i>The Economist</i> believe in? "It is to the Radicals that <i>The Economist</i> still likes to think of itself as belonging. The extreme centre is the paper\'s historical position". That is as true today as when Crowther [Geoffrey, <i>Economist</i> editor 1938\xe2\x80\x931956] said it in 1955. <i>The Economist</i> considers itself the enemy of privilege, pomposity and predictability. It has backed conservatives such as <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a>. It has supported the Americans in <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>. But it has also endorsed <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>, and espoused a variety of liberal causes: opposing capital punishment from its earliest days, while favouring penal reform and decolonisation, as well as\xe2\x80\x94more recently\xe2\x80\x94gun control and gay marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-About_us_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_us-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>In 2008, <i>The Economist</i> commented that <a href="/wiki/Cristina_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Kirchner" title="Cristina Fern\xc3\xa1ndez de Kirchner">Cristina Fern\xc3\xa1ndez de Kirchner</a>, the president of Argentina at the time was "Dashing hopes of change, Argentina\'s new president is leading her country into economic peril and social conflict".<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Economist</i> also called for <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_of_Bill_Clinton" title="Impeachment of Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton\'s impeachment</a><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> and, after the emergence of the <a href="/wiki/Abu_Ghraib_torture_and_prisoner_abuse" title="Abu Ghraib torture and prisoner abuse">Abu Ghraib torture and prisoner abuse</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> for <a href="/wiki/Donald_Rumsfeld" title="Donald Rumsfeld">Donald Rumsfeld</a>\'s resignation. Though <i>The Economist</i> initially gave vigorous support for the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">US-led invasion of Iraq</a>, it later called the operation "bungled from the start" and criticised the "almost criminal negligence" of the Bush Administration\'s handling of the war, while maintaining, in 2007, that pulling out in the short term would be irresponsible.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> In an editorial marking its 175th anniversary, <i>The Economist</i> criticised adherents to liberalism for becoming too inclined to protect the political status quo rather than pursue reform.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Economist_at_175_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Economist_at_175-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> The paper called on liberals to return to advocating for bold political, economic and social reforms: protecting <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">free markets</a>, land and tax reform in the tradition of <a href="/wiki/Georgism" title="Georgism">Georgism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Open_immigration" class="mw-redirect" title="Open immigration">open immigration</a>, a rethink of the <a href="/wiki/Social_contract" title="Social contract">social contract</a> with more emphasis on education, and a revival of <a href="/wiki/Liberal_internationalism" title="Liberal internationalism">liberal internationalism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Economist_at_175_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Economist_at_175-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Circulation">Circulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Economist&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Circulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Economist_Display.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/The_Economist_Display.jpg/220px-The_Economist_Display.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/The_Economist_Display.jpg/330px-The_Economist_Display.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/The_Economist_Display.jpg/440px-The_Economist_Display.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Economist_Display.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A display of newspapers in <a href="/wiki/Whole_Foods_Market" title="Whole Foods Market">Whole Foods</a> supermarket, depicting the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Each of <i>The Economist</i> issue\'s official date range is from Saturday to the following Friday. <i>The Economist</i> posts each week\'s new content online at approximately 2100 Thursday evening UK time, ahead of the official publication date.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> From July to December 2019, their average global <a href="/wiki/Circulation_(journal)" title="Circulation (journal)">print circulation</a> was over 909,476, while combined with their digital presence, runs to over 1.6 million.<sup id="cite_ref-pgazette_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pgazette-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> However, on a weekly average basis, the paper can reach up to 5.1 million readers, across their print and digital runs.<sup id="cite_ref-pgazette_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pgazette-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Across their social media platforms, it reaches an audience of 35 million, as of 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1877, the publication\'s circulation was 3,700, and in 1920 it had risen to 6,000. Circulation increased rapidly after 1945, reaching 100,000 by 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-About_us_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_us-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Circulation is audited by the <a href="/wiki/Audit_Bureau_of_Circulations_(UK)" title="Audit Bureau of Circulations (UK)">Audit Bureau of Circulations</a> (ABC). From around 30,000 in 1960 it has risen to near 1 million by 2000 and by 2016 to about 1.3&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Approximately half of all sales (54%) originate in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> with sales in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> making 14% of the total and continental <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> 19%.<sup id="cite_ref-gainsreaders_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gainsreaders-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Of its American readers, two out of three earn more than $100,000 a year. <i>The Economist</i> has sales, both by subscription and at newsagents, in over 200 countries.\n</p><p><i>The Economist</i> once boasted about its limited circulation. In the early 1990s it used the slogan "<i>The Economist</i> \xe2\x80\x93 not read by millions of people". "Never in the history of journalism has so much been read for so long by so few," wrote <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Crowther,_Baron_Crowther" title="Geoffrey Crowther, Baron Crowther">Geoffrey Crowther</a>, a former editor.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Censorship">Censorship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Economist&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Censorship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:234px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_page_ripped_out_from_The_Economist_by_China%27s_censorship_department_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/A_page_ripped_out_from_The_Economist_by_China%27s_censorship_department_%28cropped%29.jpg/232px-A_page_ripped_out_from_The_Economist_by_China%27s_censorship_department_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="232" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/A_page_ripped_out_from_The_Economist_by_China%27s_censorship_department_%28cropped%29.jpg/348px-A_page_ripped_out_from_The_Economist_by_China%27s_censorship_department_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/A_page_ripped_out_from_The_Economist_by_China%27s_censorship_department_%28cropped%29.jpg/464px-A_page_ripped_out_from_The_Economist_by_China%27s_censorship_department_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="2431" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_page_ripped_out_from_The_Economist_by_China%27s_censorship_department_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A page ripped out from <i>The Economist</i> by China\'s censorship department in <a href="/wiki/Liaoning_Provincial_Museum" title="Liaoning Provincial Museum">Liaoning Provincial Library</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Sections of <i>The Economist</i> criticising authoritarian regimes are frequently removed from the paper by the authorities in those countries. <i>The Economist</i> regularly has difficulties with the ruling party of Singapore, the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Action_Party" title="People&#39;s Action Party">People\'s Action Party</a>, which had successfully sued it, in a Singaporean court, for <a href="/wiki/Defamation" title="Defamation">libel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Like many other publications, <i>The Economist</i> is subjected to censorship in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> whenever it depicts a map of <a href="/wiki/Kashmir" title="Kashmir">Kashmir</a>. The maps are stamped by Indian customs officials as being "neither correct, nor authentic". Issues are sometimes delayed, but not stopped or seized.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> On 15 June 2006, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> banned the sale of <i>The Economist</i> when it published a map labelling the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a> simply as Gulf\xe2\x80\x94a choice that derives its political significance from the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf_naming_dispute" title="Persian Gulf naming dispute">Persian Gulf naming dispute</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In a separate incident, the government of <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> went further and imprisoned <i>The Economist</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s correspondent there, <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Meldrum" title="Andrew Meldrum">Andrew Meldrum</a>. The government charged him with violating a statute on "publishing untruth" for writing that a woman was decapitated by supporters of the ruling <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_African_National_Union_%E2%80%93_Patriotic_Front" class="mw-redirect" title="Zimbabwe African National Union \xe2\x80\x93 Patriotic Front">Zimbabwe African National Union \xe2\x80\x93 Patriotic Front</a> party. The <a href="/wiki/Decapitation" title="Decapitation">decapitation</a> claim was retracted<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> and allegedly fabricated by the woman\'s husband. The correspondent was later acquitted, only to receive a <a href="/wiki/Deportation" title="Deportation">deportation</a> order.\n</p><p>On 19 August 2013, <i>The Economist</i> disclosed that the Missouri Department of Corrections had censored its issue of 29 June 2013. According to the letter sent by the department, prisoners were not allowed to receive the issue because "1. it constitutes a threat to the security or discipline of the institution; 2. may facilitate or encourage criminal activity; or 3. may interfere with the rehabilitation of an offender".<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Economist&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_business_newspapers" title="List of business newspapers">List of business newspapers</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of newspapers in the United Kingdom">List of newspapers in the United Kingdom</a></li></ul>\n<div href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The title and its design are references to the book <i><a href="/wiki/No_Logo" title="No Logo">No Logo</a></i> (1999).</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
